This is a large file. I'll make the changes systematically. The key conceptual shift is that instead of separate operators (`%`, `/`, `//`), we now use `/` for all actions with `U` and `L` helpers to mark early/late phases.

<details>
<summary><code>Edit (/home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/docs/ANCHOR.md)</code></summary>

<pre><code>The file /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/docs/ANCHOR.md has been updated. Here's the result of running `cat -n` on a snippet of the edited file:
    80→
    81→These patterns have their place — large teams need boundaries, enterprise software needs flexibility. But for solo development, they're pure friction. Every layer of indirection is a place where bugs can hide and a concept you must hold in your head.
    82→
    83→Anchor actively rejects these patterns. Instead:
    84→- **Globals are available:** `an`, `E`, `X`, `U`, `L`, `A` are just there. No imports needed. You can use them from anywhere, in any file, without setup.
    85→- **Direct mutation:** Set properties directly. `self.hp = 100`. No setter methods, no signals, no observers pattern. If you want to react to a change, you check the value in your update function.
    86→- **Explicit calls:** When something happens, you call a function. `enemy:take_damage(10)`. No event buses, no implicit subscriptions, no wondering "what else triggers when this happens?"
    87→- **Zero setup:** Drop a `.ttf` in a folder and it loads. Create an object and it exists. The engine assumes you want things to work, not that you want to configure how they work.
    88→</code></pre>

</details>

<details>
<summary><code>Edit (/home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/docs/ANCHOR.md)</code></summary>

<pre><code>The file /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/docs/ANCHOR.md has been updated. Here's the result of running `cat -n` on a snippet of the edited file:
   204→---
   205→
   206→## Lifecycle
   207→
   208→### Update Order
   209→
   210→Each frame:
   211→
   212→1. **Collect all objects** — Traverse tree, gather all non-dead objects
   213→2. **Early actions** (`/ U`) — Run all early_action functions (tree order)
   214→3. **Main actions** (`/`) — Run all action functions (tree order)
   215→4. **Late actions** (`/ L`) — Run all late_action functions (tree order)
   216→5. **Cleanup** — Remove dead objects, remove dead actions, call destroy() hooks
   217→
   218→Objects created during the frame are collected in the next frame (they don't run actions in the frame they're created).
   219→
   220→### Action Phase Execution</code></pre>

</details>

<summary><code>Edit (/home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/docs/ANCHOR.md)</code></summary>

<pre><code>The file /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/docs/ANCHOR.md has been updated. Here's the result of running `cat -n` on a snippet of the edited file:
   431→## Lua Syntax Features
   432→
   433→*These features were developed after analyzing [amulet.xyz](http://amulet.xyz), Ian MacLarty's Lua game engine. Amulet uses elegant operator overloading for scene graph construction. We adapted the patterns that fit Anchor's model while rejecting those that don't (like transforms-as-nodes and coroutine-based actions).*
   434→
   435→### Operator Overview
   436→
   437→Anchor uses Lua's operator overloading to create a concise, pipeline-style syntax for object construction:
   438→
   439→| Operator | Operation | Description |
   440→|----------|-----------|-------------|
   441→| `^` | set/build | Assign properties (table) or run init code (function) |
   442→| `/` | action | Add action (runs every frame) |
   443→| `+` | add children | Add child objects to parent (parent-centric) |
   444→| `&gt;&gt;` | flow to parent | Add self to parent, **returns parent** (object-centric) |
   445→
   446→The `/` operator handles all action phases. Use the `U` and `L` helpers to mark early/late phases:
   447→
   448→| Pattern | Phase | When it runs |
   449→|---------|-------|--------------|
   450→| `/ U fn` | early | Before main actions |
   451→| `/ fn` | main | The main update phase |
   452→| `/ L fn` | late | After main actions (often drawing) |
   453→
   454→Operators are ordered by precedence (highest to lowest: `^`, then `/`, then `+`, then `&gt;&gt;`), so they chain naturally left-to-right without parentheses.
   455→
   456→### Single-Letter Aliases
   457→
   458→For elegance, Anchor provides three single-letter aliases that look like runes:</code></pre>

</details>

<details>
<summary><code>Edit (/home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/docs/ANCHOR.md)</code></summary>

<pre><code>The file /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/docs/ANCHOR.md has been updated. Here's the result of running `cat -n` on a snippet of the edited file:
   452→| `/ L fn` | late | After main actions (often drawing) |
   453→
   454→Operators are ordered by precedence (highest to lowest: `^`, then `/`, then `+`, then `&gt;&gt;`), so they chain naturally left-to-right without parentheses.
   455→
   456→### Single-Letter Aliases
   457→
   458→For elegance, Anchor provides single-letter aliases that look like runes:
   459→
   460→| Alias | Purpose | Mnemonic |
   461→|-------|---------|----------|
   462→| `E` | Object constructor | Entity |
   463→| `U` | Early action helper | Under/underlying |
   464→| `L` | Late action helper | Late |
   465→| `X` | Named action helper | eXplicit |
   466→| `A` | Query descendants | All |
   467→
   468→These are defined in the engine:
   469→
   470→```lua
   471→E = object
   472→U = function(fn) return {__early = fn} end
   473→L = function(fn) return {__late = fn} end
   474→X = function(name, fn) return {[name] = fn} end
   475→-- A is a method alias: self:A('tag') == self:all('tag')
   476→```
   477→
   478→**Future single-letter aliases** should prefer these characters, chosen for their angular, runic appearance (symmetrical, minimal roundness):
   479→
   480→```</code></pre>

</details>

   480→```
   481→E, X, A, T, L, V, U, Y, I, H

   483→
   484→### Action Helpers: `U`, `L`, and `X`
   485→
   486→The `/` operator handles all action phases. Use helpers to specify phase or name:
   487→
   488→**Phase helpers (`U` and `L`):**
   489→```lua
   490→self / U(function(self, dt) ... end)  -- early action
   491→self / function(self, dt) ... end     -- main action (default)
   492→self / L(function(self, dt) ... end)  -- late action
   493→```
   494→
   495→**Named action helper (`X`):**
   496→```lua
   497→-- Anonymous action (no name, can't be cancelled)
   498→self / function(self, dt) ... end
   499→
   500→-- Named action using X helper (self.seek points to this)
   501→self / X('seek', function(self, dt) ... end)
   502→
   503→-- Cancel later
   504→self.seek:kill()
   505→```
   506→
   507→**Combining phase and name** — use `U` or `L` with a name parameter:
   508→```lua
... [21 more lines]</code></pre>

</details>

<summary><code>Edit (/home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/docs/ANCHOR.md)</code></summary>

<pre><code>The file /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/docs/ANCHOR.md has been updated. Here's the result of running `cat -n` on a snippet of the edited file:
   540→               self:add(timer())
   541→           end
   542→```
   543→
   544→### The `/` Operator: Actions
   545→
   546→The `/` operator adds actions. Use `U` and `L` helpers to specify early/late phases:
   547→
   548→```lua
   549→object() ^ {x = 100, y = 200}
   550→         / U(function(self, dt)
   551→               -- early: runs first
   552→           end)
   553→         / function(self, dt)
   554→               -- main update
   555→               game:circle(self.x, self.y, 10, color)
   556→           end
   557→         / L(function(self, dt)
   558→               -- late: runs last, good for drawing that needs final positions
   559→           end)
   560→```
   561→
   562→Actions return `true` to remove themselves (one-shot behavior). Returning `true` only removes the action, not the object.
   563→
   564→### The `&gt;&gt;` Operator: Flow to Parent
   565→
   566→The `&gt;&gt;` operator adds the left object as a child of the right object and **returns the parent**:</code></pre>

</details>

<summary><code>Edit (/home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/docs/ANCHOR.md)</code></summary>

   632→-- Named (self.timer.flash points to this, can be killed/replaced)
   633→self.timer:after(0.15, 'flash', function() self.flashing = false end)
   634→```
   635→
   636→**Actions** can use the `U`, `L`, and `X` helpers, or methods:
   637→```lua
   638→-- Anonymous actions with phase helpers
   639→E() / U(early_fn) / update_fn / L(late_fn) &gt;&gt; arena
   640→
   641→-- Named actions with phase helpers
   642→self / U('water_sim', fn)   -- named early
   643→self / X('update', fn)      -- named main
   644→self / L('draw', fn)        -- named late
   645→
   646→-- Named with methods (alternative)
   647→self:action('update', fn)
   648→self:early_action('water_sim', fn)
   649→self:late_action('water_draw', fn)
   650→
   651→-- Cancel later
   652→self.water_sim:kill()
   653→```
   654→
   655→The helpers are simply:
   656→```lua
   657→U = function(name_or_fn, fn) ... end  -- marks early phase
   658→L = function(name_or_fn, fn) ... end  -- marks late phase
   659→X = function(name, fn) return {[name] = fn} end  -- marks name only
   660→```
... [6 more lines]</code></pre>

<pre><code>The file /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/docs/ANCHOR.md has been updated. Here's the result of running `cat -n` on a snippet of the edited file:
   765→## YueScript Alternative
   766→
   767→*YueScript (evolved from MoonScript) is a language that compiles to Lua. It offers significant syntactic improvements: significant whitespace, `@` for self, `=&gt;` for methods with implicit self, no `end` keywords, `+=`/`-=` operators, and optional parentheses. The operator-based object construction style fits YueScript's aesthetic particularly well.*
   768→
   769→### Single-Letter Aliases in YueScript
   770→
   771→The same single-letter aliases work in YueScript:
   772→
   773→```yuescript
   774→E = object                       -- Entity/object constructor
   775→U = (fn) -&gt; {__early: fn}        -- early action helper (Under)
   776→L = (fn) -&gt; {__late: fn}         -- late action helper (Late)
   777→X = (name, fn) -&gt; {[name]: fn}   -- named action helper (eXplicit)
   778→-- A is a method alias: @\A 'tag' == @\all 'tag'
   779→```
   780→
   781→### Syntax Comparison
   782→
   783→| Lua | YueScript |</code></pre>

</details>

   826→       game\circle @x, @y, 10, color
   827→   &gt;&gt; arena
   828→```
   829→

   836→
   837→    -- Named early action
   838→    @ / U 'water_sim', (dt) =&gt;
   839→      for k = 1, 8
   840→        for i = 1, @water_springs_count
   841→          -- propagate spring velocities
   842→
   843→    -- Named late action

   845→      @water_surface = {}
   846→      for spring in *@water_springs.children
   847→        -- build polyline using * iteration

   866→    @ / X 'input', (dt) =&gt;

   874→

   953→## YueScript Class System Integration
   954→
   955→Anchor uses YueScript's native class system with inheritance. This section details how the operator-based syntax integrates with YueScript classes.
   956→
   957→### Base Object Class
   958→
   959→The `object` class is the root of all game objects. It provides the core functionality and operators:
   960→
   961→```yuescript
   962→class object
   963→  -- Class-level callback: propagate metamethods to child classes
   964→  @__inherited: (child) =&gt;
   965→    -- Copy operator metamethods to child's base
   966→    for mm in *{'__pow', '__div', '__add', '__shr'}
   967→      unless rawget child.__base, mm
   968→        child.__base[mm] = @__base[mm]
   969→    -- Also propagate __inherited itself
   970→    unless rawget child, '__inherited'
   971→      child.__inherited = @@__inherited
   972→
   973→  -- Constructor
   974→  new: (name, args) =&gt;
   975→    @name = name
   976→    @children = {}
   977→    @tags = {}
   978→    @dead = false
   979→    if args
   980→      for k, v in pairs args
   981→        @[k] = v
... [148 more lines]</code></pre>

</details>

<details>
<summary><code>Edit (/home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/docs/ANCHOR.md)</code></summary>

<pre><code>The file /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/docs/ANCHOR.md has been updated. Here's the result of running `cat -n` on a snippet of the edited file:
  1213→  late_update: (dt) =&gt;
  1214→    game\circle @x, @y, @radius, @color
  1215→```
  1216→
  1217→**Methods and actions both run.** If an object has both an `update:` method and `/` actions, the method runs first, then the actions. This allows class-defined behavior to coexist with dynamically added behavior.
  1218→
  1219→Note: The `%` and `//` operators are no longer used. All actions use `/` with `U` and `L` helpers for phase selection.
  1220→
  1221→### Colliders, Springs, and Timers Are Tree Objects
  1222→
  1223→Colliders, springs, and timers are all proper tree objects (classes extending `object`). They live in `@children` like any other child, and die when their parent dies.</code></pre>

   164→---
   165→
   166→## Code Patterns
   167→
   168→### Single-Letter Aliases
   169→
   170→Anchor provides single-letter aliases that look like runes:
   171→
   172→```lua
   173→E = object                                       -- Entity/object
   174→U = function(fn) return {__early = fn} end       -- Under/early action
   175→L = function(fn) return {__late = fn} end        -- Late action
   176→X = function(name, fn) return {[name] = fn} end  -- eXplicit/named
   177→-- A is a method alias: self:A('tag') == self:all('tag')
   178→```
   179→
   180→In YueScript:
   181→```yuescript
   182→E = object
   183→U = (fn) -&gt; {__early: fn}
   184→L = (fn) -&gt; {__late: fn}
   185→X = (name, fn) -&gt; {[name]: fn}
   186→```
   187→
   188→**Future single-letter aliases** should prefer these characters, chosen for their angular, runic appearance (symmetrical, minimal roundness):
   189→
   190→```
   191→E, X, A, T, L, V, U, Y, I, H
   192→```
... [4 more lines]</code></pre>

   425→```lua

   428→    self:object('arena', args)
   429→    self:setup_physics()

<pre><code>The file /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/.claude/CLAUDE.md has been updated. Here's the result of running `cat -n` on a snippet of the edited file:
   493→      end)

   496→
   497→**Multiple `^` operators:** When chaining multiple `^`, group all initialization before action operators:
   498→```lua
   499→-- Good: all init together, then actions
   500→E() ^ {x = 100, y = 200}
   501→   ^ function(self) self + timer() end
   502→   / function(self, dt) ... end
   503→   &gt;&gt; arena
   504→
   505→-- Bad: init split across the chain
   506→E() ^ {x = 100}
   507→   / function(self, dt) ... end
   508→   ^ function(self) self + timer() end -- init after action, harder to follow
   509→   &gt;&gt; arena
   510→```
   511→
   512→### Named vs Anonymous
   513→
   514→The tree automatically manages named children: adding a child with a name that already exists kills the old child first. This provides cancellation and replacement without explicit tag systems.</code></pre>

</details>

   694→    if self.water_sim then self.water_sim:kill() end

<summary><code>Edit (/home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/.claude/CLAUDE.md)</code></summary>

<pre><code>The file /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/.claude/CLAUDE.md has been updated. Here's the result of running `cat -n` on a snippet of the edited file:
   821→#### No Bureaucracy
   822→
   823→Imports, exports, dependency injection, configuration objects, registration systems — these are bureaucracy. They may be necessary in large teams, but for solo development they're friction.
   824→
   825→Anchor prefers:
   826→- Globals that are just available (`an`, `E`, `U`, `L`, `X`, `A`)
   827→- Direct mutation over message passing
   828→- Explicit calls over implicit event systems
   829→- Things that work without setup
   830→
   831→**When evaluating features:** Does this require ceremony to use, or does it just work?
   832→
   833→#### Alien But Right</code></pre>

</details>

<details>
<summary><code>Edit (/home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/.claude/CLAUDE.md)</code></summary>

<pre><code>The file /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/.claude/CLAUDE.md has been updated. Here's the result of running `cat -n` on a snippet of the edited file:
   829→- Things that work without setup
   830→
   831→**When evaluating features:** Does this require ceremony to use, or does it just work?
   832→
   833→#### Alien But Right
   834→
   835→The operator syntax (`^`, `/`, `+`, `&gt;&gt;`) and single-letter aliases (`E`, `U`, `L`, `X`, `A`) are deliberately unusual. Inspired by Hoon's rune system — symbols that seem foreign at first but become natural with use.
   836→
   837→The goal isn't familiarity, it's terseness and visual distinctiveness. `E 'player'` is weirder than `Object.new('player')` but it's shorter and once learned, instantly recognizable.
   838→
   839→Single-letter aliases follow a preference for angular, symmetrical letters: E, X, A, T, L, V, U, Y, I, H. Avoid round letters (O, Q, C, G).
   840→
   841→**When evaluating features:** Does this earn its complexity? Is the weirdness worth it?
   842→
   843→### Language Boundary Philosophy</code></pre>

</details>

<pre><code>1→# Anchor Implementation Plan
     2→
     3→C engine with YueScript scripting, OpenGL rendering, targeting Windows, Linux, and Web.
     4→
     5→---
     6→
     7→## Summary of Key Decisions
     8→
     9→| Area | Decision | Rationale |
    10→|------|----------|-----------|
    11→| Renderer | OpenGL | Smooth rotation, additive blending, performance headroom, console-portable |
    12→| Audio | TBD (miniaudio or SoLoud) | Need pitch shifting; SDL_mixer insufficient |
    13→| Physics | Box2D 3.1 | Already used, true ball-to-ball collisions needed |
    14→| Scripting | Lua 5.4 + YueScript | Build-time compilation with `-r` flag for line numbers |
    15→| Timestep | Fixed 60fps | Determinism matters for potential replay support |
    16→| Resolution | Per-game configurable | 480×270, 640×360, or custom; integer scaling |
    17→| C Structure | Single anchor.c | Monolithic file, easier navigation |
    18→| Resources | Live forever | Games are small enough; no unloading needed |
    19→| Distribution | Single executable | Assets embedded |
    20→
    21→---
    22→
    23→## Build Strategy
    24→
    25→### YueScript Compilation
    26→
    27→**Build-time compilation** — compile `.yue` → `.lua` during build, not at runtime.
    28→
    29→```
    30→game.yue ──► yue -r ──► game.lua ──► embedded in executable

   479→- Constructor with name/args
   480→- Tree operations: `add_child`, `remove_child`, `kill`
   481→- Tagging: `tag`, `is`, `all` / `A`
   482→- Links: `link` for horizontal dependencies
   483→- Operators: `^`, `%`, `/`, `//`, `+`, `&gt;&gt;`
   484→- `__inherited` hook to propagate operators to child classes
   485→
   486→**Ask developer before implementing details.**
   487→
   488→### Engine Object Pattern
   489→
   490→Timer, spring, and collider are examples of **engine objects** — classes that wrap C-side resources. All engine objects follow this pattern:
   491→
   492→1. They extend the base `object` class
   493→2. They're instantiated and added as children: `@ + timer()`
   494→3. They're named after themselves by default (e.g., `timer()` has `name = 'timer'`)
   495→4. Parent accesses them via that name: `@timer:after(...)`
   496→5. They implement `destroy()` to clean up C-side resources when killed
   497→
   498→This pattern applies to any future engine objects (particles, audio sources, etc.).
   499→
... [111 more lines]</code></pre>

</details>

> `Bash (mv /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/yue/operator_comparison.yue /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/y...)`

Done. All three documents have been updated to reflect the new operator system:

**Summary of changes:**

| Old | New |
|-----|-----|
| `%` operator for early actions | `/ U(fn)` or `/ U('name', fn)` |
| `//` operator for late actions | `/ L(fn)` or `/ L('name', fn)` |
| `__mod` and `__idiv` metamethods | Single `__div` that detects U/L/X helpers |

**New alias set:**
- **E** = object (Entity)
- **U** = early action helper (Under/underlying)
- **L** = late action helper (Late)
- **X** = named action helper (eXplicit)
- **A** = all() query method alias (All)

**Files updated:**
- `docs/ANCHOR.md` — operator tables, examples, reference implementation
- `docs/ANCHOR_IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md` — Phase 10 specifications
- `.claude/CLAUDE.md` — code patterns, aliases, context brief
- `yue/examples.yue` — renamed from operator_comparison.yue, cleaned up header

> Please remove all mentions of % and //, in one section you mention that they're no longer used, but anyone reading the documents doesn't need that information about the past.

> I think that was the only problem that you mentioned that I thought we had to fix. Great, anything else you have to say about the engine that you feel is wrong?

Looking back through everything, I think the design is solid now. The main issues we addressed were:

1. **`add_child` → `add`** — Fixed the method name inconsistency
2. **`%` and `//` → `/ U` and `/ L`** — Unified all actions under `/` with helpers

One minor thing I noticed but didn't flag: the "Single-Letter Aliases" section shows simplified definitions:

```lua
U = function(fn) return {__early = fn} end
L = function(fn) return {__late = fn} end
```

But the actual usage supports two forms: `U(fn)` and `U('name', fn)`. The full implementation in the reference section handles both, but the overview only shows the single-argument form.

This is probably fine — the overview is meant to be simple, and the "Action Helpers" section explains the full usage. But if you want complete accuracy in the overview, the signatures would be:

```lua
U = function(name_or_fn, fn) ... end  -- supports U(fn) or U('name', fn)
L = function(name_or_fn, fn) ... end  -- supports L(fn) or L('name', fn)
```

Other than that, I don't see any remaining issues. The philosophy is coherent, the tree model is elegant, the operator syntax is consistent, and the documentation matches the reference implementation.

> Please correct that issue.

<pre><code>The file /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/docs/ANCHOR.md has been updated. Here's the result of running `cat -n` on a snippet of the edited file:
   464→| `L` | Late action helper | Late |
   465→| `X` | Named action helper | eXplicit |
   466→| `A` | Query descendants | All |
   467→
   468→These are defined in the engine:
   469→
   470→```lua
   471→E = object
   472→U = function(name_or_fn, fn) ... end  -- U(fn) or U('name', fn)
   473→L = function(name_or_fn, fn) ... end  -- L(fn) or L('name', fn)
   474→X = function(name, fn) return {[name] = fn} end
   475→-- A is a method alias: self:A('tag') == self:all('tag')
   476→```
   477→
   478→**Future single-letter aliases** should prefer these characters, chosen for their angular, runic appearance (symmetrical, minimal roundness):
   479→
   480→```</code></pre>

<summary><code>Edit (/home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/.claude/CLAUDE.md)</code></summary>

<pre><code>The file /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/.claude/CLAUDE.md has been updated. Here's the result of running `cat -n` on a snippet of the edited file:
   168→### Single-Letter Aliases
   169→
   170→Anchor provides single-letter aliases that look like runes:
   171→
   172→```lua
   173→E = object                                        -- Entity/object
   174→U = function(name_or_fn, fn) ... end              -- U(fn) or U('name', fn)
   175→L = function(name_or_fn, fn) ... end              -- L(fn) or L('name', fn)
   176→X = function(name, fn) return {[name] = fn} end   -- eXplicit/named
   177→-- A is a method alias: self:A('tag') == self:all('tag')
   178→```
   179→
   180→In YueScript:
   181→```yuescript
   182→E = object
   183→U = (name_or_fn, fn) -&gt; ...  -- U(fn) or U('name', fn)
   184→L = (name_or_fn, fn) -&gt; ...  -- L(fn) or L('name', fn)
   185→X = (name, fn) -&gt; {[name]: fn}
   186→```
   187→
   188→**Future single-letter aliases** should prefer these characters, chosen for their angular, runic appearance (symmetrical, minimal roundness):
   189→
   190→```</code></pre>

<pre><code>The file /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/docs/ANCHOR.md has been updated. Here's the result of running `cat -n` on a snippet of the edited file:
   767→*YueScript (evolved from MoonScript) is a language that compiles to Lua. It offers significant syntactic improvements: significant whitespace, `@` for self, `=&gt;` for methods with implicit self, no `end` keywords, `+=`/`-=` operators, and optional parentheses. The operator-based object construction style fits YueScript's aesthetic particularly well.*
   768→
   769→### Single-Letter Aliases in YueScript
   770→
   771→The same single-letter aliases work in YueScript:
   772→
   773→```yuescript
   774→E = object                        -- Entity/object constructor
   775→U = (name_or_fn, fn) -&gt; ...       -- U(fn) or U('name', fn)
   776→L = (name_or_fn, fn) -&gt; ...       -- L(fn) or L('name', fn)
   777→X = (name, fn) -&gt; {[name]: fn}    -- named action helper (eXplicit)
   778→-- A is a method alias: @\A 'tag' == @\all 'tag'
   779→```
   780→
   781→### Syntax Comparison
   782→
   783→| Lua | YueScript |</code></pre>

<pre><code>500→  1361→layer:draw_text('99', 'large', x, y, r, sx, sy)  -- with optional transform
   501→  1362→```
   502→  1363→
   503→  1364→---
   504→  1365→
   505→  1366→## Rendering Architecture
   506→  1367→
   507→  1368→### Software Renderer
   508→  1369→
   509→  1370→Anchor uses a CPU-based software renderer targeting 480×270 or 640×360 resolution (depending on game). This approach provides direct pixel manipulation, simpler debugging, and consistent behavior across platforms.
   510→  1371→
   511→  1372→### Layers = Framebuffers
   512→  1373→
   513→  1374→Each layer is a framebuffer. Draw commands are batched per layer and flushed at end of frame:
   514→  1375→
   515→  1376→1. Lua calls `layer:circle()`, `layer:draw_image()`, etc.
   516→  1377→2. Each call appends to that layer's command buffer
   517→  1378→3. At end of frame, C processes all commands in a tight loop
   518→  1379→4. Effects are applied per-layer (C functions, configured from Lua)
   519→  1380→5. Layers composite to screen via alpha blending
   520→  1381→
   521→  1382→### Sprites
   522→  1383→
   523→  1384→Sprites use precomputed rotations (16 or 32 angles) with runtime scaling. This trades memory for computation and creates a distinctive aesthetic with discrete rotation angles.
   524→  1385→
   525→  1386→### Effects
   526→  1387→
   527→  1388→Post-processing effects are implemented in C and configured from Lua:
   528→  1389→
   529→... [180 more lines]&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;

>    - Minor style issue with build function using `self:add(timer())` instead of `+`

> 3. **User feedback on add/add_child**: User said "There should be no alias, it should just be the add function, no add_child, any usages of it must be wrong for some reason."
> 
> 4. **High-level engine analysis** - User asked for my opinion on the engine design. I provided detailed analysis of:
>    - Locality principle - genuinely achieved
>    - No bureaucracy - achieved
>    - Tree-based ownership - elegant core insight
>    - Alien but right syntax - mostly achieved, but noted `//` and `%` operators were arbitrary
> 
> 5. **Operator redesign discussion** - User asked about changing `%` and `//` operators. Constraints:
>    - Bound to Lua/YueScript operators
>    - Precedence matters for chaining
>    - Available at same precedence as `/`: `*`, `/`, `//`, `%`
> 
> 6. **First proposal**: Use `*` for early, `/` for main, `%` for late (based on "remainder" mnemonic for late)
> 
> 7. **User asked about modifier approach**: Could all actions use `/` with modifiers?
> 
> 8. **Created comparison file** - Created `/home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/yue/operator_comparison.yue` showing two approaches:
>    - U/L helpers: `/ U fn`, `/ fn`, `/ L fn`
>    - X prefix: `/ X '<', fn`, `/ fn`, `/ X '>', fn`
> 
> 9. **Iterative alias exploration** - User tried multiple letter combinations:
>    - E for early, A for object → but A was used for `all()` query
>    - E for early, Y for object
>    - E for early, T for object (Thing)
>    - E for early, X for object, N for named
>    - **Final decision**: E for object, U for early, L for late, X for named, A for all
> 
> 10. **Documentation updates** - Updated all three files to reflect new operator system:
>     - Changed `%` operator to `/ U(fn)` pattern
>     - Changed `//` operator to `/ L(fn)` pattern
>     - Updated reference implementation to use single `__div` that detects U/L/X helpers
>     - Updated all code examples
> 
> 11. **Removed deprecated mentions** - User asked to remove all mentions of `%` and `//` including the note about them being deprecated
> 
> 12. **Final fix** - Updated simplified alias definitions to show correct signatures:
>     - `U = function(name_or_fn, fn) ... end` (supports both `U(fn)` and `U('name', fn)`)
>     - `L = function(name_or_fn, fn) ... end`
>

> The final alias set is:
> - E = object (Entity)
> - U = early action helper (Under/underlying)
> - L = late action helper (Late)
> - X = named action helper (eXplicit)
> - A = all() query method alias (All)

> Summary:
> 1. Primary Request and Intent:
>    - Run a thorough consistency check on all documentation files (ANCHOR.md, ANCHOR_IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md, CLAUDE.md)
>    - Provide high-level analysis/opinion on the engine design
>    - Redesign the action phase operators (`%` for early, `//` for late) to use a unified `/` operator with helper functions
>    - Explore multiple single-letter alias combinations for object constructor and action helpers
>    - Update all documentation to reflect the new operator system
>    - End the session with a detailed summary reading the full transcript due to multiple compactions
> 
> 2. Key Technical Concepts:
>    - **Unified action operator**: All actions now use `/` with `U` (early) and `L` (late) helpers instead of separate `%` and `//` operators
>    - **Single-letter aliases**: E (object), U (early), L (late), X (named), A (all query) - all from runic set
>    - **Helper function signatures**: `U` and `L` support both `U(fn)` and `U('name', fn)` forms
>    - **`__div` operator overload**: Single operator detects `__early`, `__late`, or named action patterns
>    - **Engine object pattern**: Timer, spring, collider are tree objects named after themselves by default
>    - **Tree-based ownership**: Parent dies → children die automatically
>    - **Operator precedence**: `^` (highest), then `/`, then `+`, then `>>` (lowest)
> 
> 3. Files and Code Sections:
>    - **`/home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/docs/ANCHOR.md`**
>      - Core specification document - all operator tables, examples, and reference implementation updated
>      - Changed operator overview to show `/` with `U`/`L` helpers
>      - Updated Single-Letter Aliases section:
>        ```lua
>        E = object
>        U = function(name_or_fn, fn) ... end  -- U(fn) or U('name', fn)
>        L = function(name_or_fn, fn) ... end  -- L(fn) or L('name', fn)
>        X = function(name, fn) return {[name] = fn} end
>        ```
>      - Updated `__div` operator in reference implementation to detect phase helpers
>      - Removed mentions of `%` and `//` operators
> 
>    - **`/home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/docs/ANCHOR_IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md`**
>      - Implementation roadmap - updated Phase 10 specifications
>      - Changed tree operations from `add_child` to `add`
>      - Updated operators list: `^`, `/`, `+`, `>>`
>      - Added phase helpers: `U` (early), `L` (late), `X` (named)
>      - Updated alias definitions:
>        ```yuescript
>        E = object
>        U = (name_or_fn, fn) -> if fn then {__early: name_or_fn, __fn: fn} else {__early: name_or_fn}
>        L = (name_or_fn, fn) -> if fn then {__late: name_or_fn, __fn: fn} else {__late: name_or_fn}
>        X = (name, fn) -> {[name]: fn}
>        ```
> 
>    - **`/home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/.claude/CLAUDE.md`**
>      - Guidelines for Claude - updated code patterns and context brief
>      - Updated all action examples to use `/ U()` and `/ L()` pattern
>      - Updated globals list to include U and L
>      - Changed operator syntax description from `^`, `/`, `%`, `//` to `^`, `/`, `+`, `>>`

<pre><code>500→  1361→layer:draw_text('99', 'large', x, y, r, sx, sy)  -- with optional transform
   501→  1362→```
   502→  1363→
   503→  1364→---
   504→  1365→
   505→  1366→## Rendering Architecture
   506→  1367→
   507→  1368→### Software Renderer
   508→  1369→
   509→  1370→Anchor uses a CPU-based software renderer targeting 480×270 or 640×360 resolution (depending on game). This approach provides direct pixel manipulation, simpler debugging, and consistent behavior across platforms.
   510→  1371→
   511→  1372→### Layers = Framebuffers
   512→  1373→
   513→  1374→Each layer is a framebuffer. Draw commands are batched per layer and flushed at end of frame:
   514→  1375→
   515→  1376→1. Lua calls `layer:circle()`, `layer:draw_image()`, etc.
   516→  1377→2. Each call appends to that layer's command buffer
   517→  1378→3. At end of frame, C processes all commands in a tight loop
   518→  1379→4. Effects are applied per-layer (C functions, configured from Lua)
   519→  1380→5. Layers composite to screen via alpha blending
   520→  1381→
   521→  1382→### Sprites
   522→  1383→
   523→  1384→Sprites use precomputed rotations (16 or 32 angles) with runtime scaling. This trades memory for computation and creates a distinctive aesthetic with discrete rotation angles.
   524→  1385→
   525→  1386→### Effects
   526→  1387→
   527→  1388→Post-processing effects are implemented in C and configured from Lua:
   528→  1389→
   529→... [180 more lines]&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;
... [470 more lines]</code></pre>

<pre><code>5300→- Named versions need separate helpers: `/ U 'physics', (dt) =&gt;`, `/ L 'draw', (dt) =&gt;`
  5301→- Introduces two new single-letter globals (U and L)
  5302→
  5303→**X prefix approach:**
  5304→- Anonymous early/late require X: `/ X '&lt;', (dt) =&gt;` — more verbose
  5305→- Named versions are compact: `/ X '&lt;physics', (dt) =&gt;` — the prefix is part of the name
  5306→- Reuses existing X helper, no new globals
  5307→- The `&lt;` and `&gt;` have natural "before/after" meaning (arrows pointing left/right on a timeline)
  5308→
  5309→The tradeoff is basically:
  5310→- **U/L**: Cleaner for anonymous actions, but adds two globals
  5311→- **X prefix**: More verbose for anonymous, but unified under one mechanism
  5312→
  5313→&gt; We could use E for early and another letter for object itself. What do you think?

---

**Title:** Unified Action Operators

**Summary:**

This session focused on a major redesign of Anchor's action phase operators and comprehensive documentation consistency fixes.

**Operator Redesign:**
- Replaced the arbitrary `%` (early) and `//` (late) operators with a unified `/` operator using phase helpers
- Explored multiple single-letter alias combinations: A/E (A conflicted with `all()`), Y/E, T/E, X/N before settling on final set
- Final aliases: E (object/Entity), U (early/Under), L (late/Late), X (named/eXplicit), A (all query/All)
- All aliases are runic (angular, symmetrical) with decent mnemonics
- `/` operator now detects `U`, `L`, and `X` helpers via `__early`, `__late`, or string key patterns
- Helper signatures support both anonymous and named forms: `U(fn)` and `U('name', fn)`

**Documentation Consistency (from pre-compaction work):**
- Fixed timer architecture: timer is a child object with `after`, `every`, `tween` methods, accessed via `self.timer:after(...)`
- Documented engine object pattern: timer/spring/collider are tree objects named after themselves by default
- Fixed spring examples: single springs use `spring(1, 200, 10)` → `self.spring`, multiples use explicit names
- Fixed collider naming: optional name parameter separate from physics tag
- Simplified color format: `an.colors.white` without `[0]` indexing
- Updated platforms: Linux as primary alongside Windows and Web
- Changed `add_child` → `add` in reference implementation

**High-Level Engine Analysis:**
- Confirmed locality principle is genuinely achieved through operator pipeline syntax
- Confirmed no-bureaucracy goal achieved via globals and automatic cleanup
- Identified tree-based ownership as the core elegant insight
- Noted collision handling and draw order are necessary tradeoffs that break locality
- Critiqued `%` and `//` as arbitrary, which led to the redesign

**Files updated:**
- ANCHOR.md: operators, aliases, reference implementation, all examples
- ANCHOR_IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md: Phase 10 operators, alias definitions
- CLAUDE.md: code patterns, globals list, all examples
- Created yue/examples.yue with complete operator examples

**Title:** OpenGL Decision & Unified Operators

**Summary:**

This session covered a comprehensive implementation plan interview, the OpenGL renderer decision, and a major redesign of action phase operators.

**Implementation Plan Interview:**
- Conducted detailed interview using AskUserQuestion tool about engine requirements
- Discussed software renderer vs OpenGL tradeoffs extensively:
  - Motivations for software renderer: aesthetic, simplicity, web reliability
  - But: discrete rotation was only "acceptable tradeoff" (not desired), additive blending is essential
  - Console targets (Switch, Xbox, PS) require GPU APIs — incompatible with software rendering
  - You already know GLSL (500+ line shaders), the concern was preference not capability
- **Final decision: OpenGL** — clean decision, no "software-like mental model" compromise
- Audio: SDL_mixer insufficient (no pitch shifting), needs research (miniaudio vs SoLoud)
- Physics: Box2D 3.x confirmed, fixed 60fps timestep for determinism
- Platform targets: Windows, Linux, Web primary; mobile/console if games succeed
- Debug workflow: print debugging + error screen sufficient
- Resolution: per-game configurable (480×270, 640×360, etc.)
- C structure: single `anchor.c` file, resources live forever, single executable distribution
- Distant artistic vision: "7 stories that are 7 games" with merged game/narrative elements requiring pixel-level control HTML can't provide

**Documentation Updates:**
- Created new `ANCHOR_IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md` with OpenGL, 10 phases, TBD audio
- Deleted old `IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md` (software renderer based)
- Updated ANCHOR.md: removed software renderer sections, added OpenGL rendering section
- Updated CLAUDE.md: changed references from software rendering to OpenGL

**Consistency Fixes (from multiple compaction rounds):**
- Timer architecture: child object with `after`, `every`, `tween` methods via `self.timer:after(...)`
- Engine object pattern: timer/spring/collider are tree objects named after themselves by default
- Spring examples: single springs use `spring(1, 200, 10)` → `self.spring`
- Collider naming: optional name parameter separate from physics tag
- Color format: `an.colors.white` without `[0]` indexing
- Platforms: Linux as primary alongside Windows and Web
- Changed `add_child` → `add` in reference implementation

**Operator Redesign:**
- Replaced arbitrary `%` (early) and `//` (late) operators with unified `/` operator using phase helpers
- Explored alias combinations: A/E, Y/E, T/E, X/N before final decision
- **Final aliases:** E (object/Entity), U (early/Under), L (late/Late), X (named/eXplicit), A (all query/All)
- All runic (angular, symmetrical letters), all with decent mnemonics
- `/` operator detects `U`, `L`, and `X` helpers via `__early`, `__late`, or string key patterns
- Updated all three documentation files with new operator syntax

**High-Level Engine Analysis:**
- Confirmed locality principle genuinely achieved through operator pipeline
- Confirmed no-bureaucracy goal achieved via globals and automatic cleanup
- Tree-based ownership identified as core elegant insight
- Collision handling and draw order are necessary tradeoffs that break locality

---

**Title:** OpenGL Decision & Unified Operators

**Summary:**

This session began with a comprehensive interview to improve the implementation plan, leading to a major renderer decision, followed by consistency fixes and an operator redesign.

**Implementation Plan Interview:**
- Conducted detailed interview using AskUserQuestion tool covering all engine requirements
- Software renderer motivations discussed: aesthetic, simplicity, web reliability
- Key discoveries that changed the calculus:
  - Discrete rotation was only "acceptable tradeoff" — not a desired aesthetic
  - Additive blending is essential (explosions, energy effects)
  - Console targets (Switch, Xbox, PlayStation) require GPU APIs — incompatible with software rendering
  - You already know GLSL and have written 500+ line shaders; the concern was preference, not capability
  - Pixel control examples were mostly theoretical (Noita-style) rather than needed for ball combat games
- Audio gap identified: SDL_mixer insufficient (no pitch shifting), needs research (miniaudio vs SoLoud)
- Physics confirmed: Box2D 3.x, fixed 60fps timestep for determinism
- Platform targets: Windows, Linux, Web primary; mobile/console if games succeed
- Debug workflow: print debugging + error screen sufficient
- C structure: single `anchor.c`, resources live forever, single executable distribution
- Distant artistic vision revealed: "7 stories that are 7 games" with merged game/narrative elements
- **Final decision: OpenGL** — clean decision with no "software-like mental model" compromise

**Documentation Updates:**
- Created new `ANCHOR_IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md` with OpenGL, 10 phases, TBD audio
- Deleted old `IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md` (software renderer based)
- Updated ANCHOR.md: removed software renderer sections (~200 lines), added OpenGL rendering
- Updated CLAUDE.md: changed references from software rendering to OpenGL

**Consistency Fixes (multiple rounds, including pre-compaction work):**
- Timer architecture: child object with `after`, `every`, `tween` methods via `self.timer:after(...)`
- Engine object pattern: timer/spring/collider are tree objects named after themselves by default
- Spring examples: single springs use `spring(1, 200, 10)` → `self.spring`; multiples use explicit names
- Collider naming: optional name parameter separate from physics tag
- Color format: `an.colors.white` without `[0]` indexing
- Platforms: Linux as primary alongside Windows and Web
- Changed `add_child` → `add` in reference implementation
- Build function example: `self:add(timer())` → `self + timer()`

**High-Level Engine Analysis:**
- Confirmed locality principle genuinely achieved through operator pipeline
- Confirmed no-bureaucracy goal achieved via globals and automatic cleanup
- Tree-based ownership identified as core elegant insight
- Collision handling and draw order noted as necessary tradeoffs that break locality
- Critiqued `%` and `//` operators as arbitrary with no mnemonic — led to redesign

**Operator Redesign:**
- Replaced arbitrary `%` (early) and `//` (late) with unified `/` operator using phase helpers
- Explored multiple alias combinations: A/E (A conflicted with `all()`), Y/E, T/E, X/N
- **Final aliases:** E (object/Entity), U (early/Under), L (late/Late), X (named/eXplicit), A (all/All)
- All runic (angular, symmetrical letters), all with decent mnemonics
- `/` operator detects `U`, `L`, and `X` helpers via `__early`, `__late`, or string key patterns
- Helper signatures support both forms: `U(fn)` and `U('name', fn)`
- Updated all three documentation files with new operator syntax

**Final Cleanup:**
- Removed all mentions of deprecated `%` and `//` operators
- Fixed simplified alias definitions to show full signatures

**Files modified:**
- Created: `docs/ANCHOR_IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md`
- Deleted: `docs/IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md`

- Created: `yue/examples.yue` (renamed from `operator_comparison.yue`)

- Key discoveries: discrete rotation was acceptable tradeoff not desired aesthetic; additive blending essential; console targets require GPU APIs; already know GLSL (500+ line shaders)
- Audio gap identified: SDL_mixer insufficient (no pitch shifting), needs research
- Final decision: OpenGL — clean decision with no software-like mental model compromise

Documentation Updates:
- Created new ANCHOR_IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md with OpenGL, 10 phases, TBD audio
- Deleted old IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md (software renderer based)
- Updated ANCHOR.md and CLAUDE.md to remove software renderer references

Consistency Fixes:
- Timer architecture: child object with after/every/tween methods via self.timer:after(...)
- Engine object pattern: timer/spring/collider named after themselves by default
- Spring examples: single springs use spring(1, 200, 10) → self.spring
- Changed add_child → add in reference implementation

Operator Redesign:
- Replaced % (early) and // (late) with unified / operator using phase helpers
- Final aliases: E (object), U (early), L (late), X (named), A (all)
- Helper signatures support both U(fn) and U('name', fn) forms

Co-Authored-By: Claude &lt;noreply@anthropic.com&gt;</code></pre>

<pre><code>Anchor Interview

## Summary

This session began with a comprehensive interview to improve the implementation plan, leading to a major renderer decision, followed by consistency fixes and an operator redesign.

**Implementation Plan Interview:**
- Conducted detailed interview using AskUserQuestion tool covering all engine requirements
- Software renderer motivations discussed: aesthetic, simplicity, web reliability
- Key discoveries that changed the calculus:
  - Discrete rotation was only "acceptable tradeoff" — not a desired aesthetic
  - Additive blending is essential (explosions, energy effects)
  - Console targets (Switch, Xbox, PlayStation) require GPU APIs — incompatible with software rendering
  - You already know GLSL and have written 500+ line shaders; the concern was preference, not capability
  - Pixel control examples were mostly theoretical (Noita-style) rather than needed for ball combat games
- Audio gap identified: SDL_mixer insufficient (no pitch shifting), needs research (miniaudio vs SoLoud)
- Physics confirmed: Box2D 3.x, fixed 60fps timestep for determinism
- Platform targets: Windows, Linux, Web primary; mobile/console if games succeed
- Debug workflow: print debugging + error screen sufficient
- C structure: single `anchor.c`, resources live forever, single executable distribution
- Distant artistic vision revealed: "7 stories that are 7 games" with merged game/narrative elements
- **Final decision: OpenGL** — clean decision with no "software-like mental model" compromise

**Documentation Updates:**
- Created new `ANCHOR_IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md` with OpenGL, 10 phases, TBD audio
- Deleted old `IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md` (software renderer based)
- Updated ANCHOR.md: removed software renderer sections (~200 lines), added OpenGL rendering
- Updated CLAUDE.md: changed references from software rendering to OpenGL

**Consistency Fixes (multiple rounds, including pre-compaction work):**</code></pre>
